  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fbff0c84-6108-4bb0-a90b-faf4c345692a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2065102862561586298"><b>
  <i>It's time to choose sides....</i>
</b><br/><br/>On the surface, Sorry-in-the-Vale is a sleepy English town. But Kami Glass knows the truth. Sorry-in-the-Vale is full of magic.   <span id="freeText2065102862561586298" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>It's time to choose sides....</i>
</b><br /><br />On the surface, Sorry-in-the-Vale is a sleepy English town. But Kami Glass knows the truth. Sorry-in-the-Vale is full of magic. In the old days, the Lynburn family ruled with fear, terrifying the people into submission in order to kill for blood and power. Now the Lynburns are back, and Rob Lynburn is gathering sorcerers so that the town can return to the old ways.<br /><br />But Rob and his followers aren’t the only sorcerers in town. A decision must be made: pay the blood sacrifice, or fight. For Kami, this means more than just choosing between good and evil. With her link to Jared Lynburn severed, she’s now free to love anyone she chooses. But who should that be?<br /><br />A darkly humorous take on Gothic romance, Sarah Rees Brennan's Lynburn Legacy weaves together the tale of a heroine desperate to protect those she loves, two boys hoping to be saved, and the magical forces that will shape their destiny.</span>

<div id="review_415140662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415140662" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415140662?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=arc-galley-and-first-reads">arc-galley-and-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415140662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13876024016317670534">In retrospect, <i>Untold</i> is an extraordinarily boring novel. <i>Unspoken</i> was a novel I loved inexplicably; just because it was whimsical and amusing and magical and I could. With <i>Untold,</i> however, my feelings are far more mixed. On one hand, this novel delivered exactly what I wanted it to, but on another, I found myself left with an intangible wanting. <br/><br/>What Brennan has always excelled at - ever since the release of her debut - is capturing the personality behind the shells her characters wear. Kami, e</span>
  <span id="freeText13876024016317670534" style="display:none">In retrospect, <i>Untold</i> is an extraordinarily boring novel. <i>Unspoken</i> was a novel I loved inexplicably; just because it was whimsical and amusing and magical and I could. With <i>Untold,</i> however, my feelings are far more mixed. On one hand, this novel delivered exactly what I wanted it to, but on another, I found myself left with an intangible wanting. <br /><br />What Brennan has always excelled at - ever since the release of her debut - is capturing the personality behind the shells her characters wear. Kami, especially, truly blooms in this installment. Without her link to Jared, she is suddenly forced to face her deepest fears and secret hopes - alone. Moreover, her once-perfect family suddenly cracks under the pressure of magic as truths come spilling out. For me, the highlight of this novel lies in seeing Kami come to believe in herself, all while retaining her characteristic flair. I also really loved her interactions with her parents. Kami, as a half-Japanese character, is treated as such and the background on her parents, not to mention the close ties between her siblings, is written so deftly, weaving this family both together and apart. <br /><br /><i>Untold</i> would be nothing, though, without its secondary characters. Brennan truly delves into the mindset of Kami's friends, making their lives and troubles just as real for us as Kami's. Yet, where this concept falters is in its execution. While I've come away from <i>Untold</i> truly understanding the layers behind characters such as Angela, Holly, or Ash, beyond adding more depth to the story, their perspectives did little. Ultimately, the relationships between these secondary characters has progressed very little. I surmise that - hopefully - we'll see them play a much greater role in <i>Unbroken</i> and all the backstory Brennan has written will finally come into play, but with this installment, it's rather useless. <br /><br />I find that the issue with <i>Untold</i> lies there. Its plot is so very loose and flimsy. It's meant to be centered around Kami learning to fight back against the sorcerers, but it's composed of conversation, drama, and tension. It's certainly enjoyable, but it lacks a certain tightness to its motivations that its predecessor possessed. Moreover, I desperately longed for more; more about the magic of the Lynburns, more about Rob than just a facade of black-and-white evil, more of the classic atmosphere that Sorry-in-the-Vale possessed in <i>Unspoken.</i> Just...more.<br /><br />(Just Jared!) You didn't think I'd end this review without mentioning Jared or Rusty, did you? ;) Rusty, as always, is a delight with his laugh-out-loud dialogue and hidden depths - which still remain hidden. Jared, however, becomes ever more real as the novel progresses. I love the few glimpses we're given into his mind - heart-breaking, but necessary - and am really impressed by the moral ambiguity associated with this character. His affection for Kami is no secret, but neither is his desire for the link, which puts him in an ironic situation. Furthermore, Brennan brings up another level of interest as she forces us to question whether Jared would be Jared without Kami in his head. It's interesting, merely because Jared is so very fixated upon Kami and does contain his own dark patches. He really does steal the show whenever he turns up on the page, though, and I really love that both he and Kami retain their own auras, despite their tight bond.<br /><br />Ultimately, I can't say that <i>Untold</i> shows much plot progression, but it's entertaining nevertheless. I both love and hate that there's such a strong focus on character development in this novel, only because much of it failed to have much direction, but Brennan manages to keep us riveted with her every word and it's physically painful to leave behind these characters as we leave our hearts behind too. <i>Untold</i> isn't one of Brennan's best works, but it'll keep you coming back for more. (What? You thought Brennan wouldn't write another cliffhanger? You naive reader...you're in for a shock with these last few pages. And we thought <i>Unspoken</i> was bad... *shakes head*)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13876024016317670534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_615007480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615007480" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615007480?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=uk">uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=awesome-guy">awesome-guy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615007480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6970554168934859704"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><br/><br/><b>I usually hate love triangles, I usually hate the romance. This book is different in that I actually enjoyed both.</b> I felt the love triangle was complex enough, the romance and relationships between the characters were beautifully, realistically portrayed. This book had a tremendous amount of humor. It had an amazing, strong main character. The side characters were compelling; funny, flawed, loveable. It portrayed a lesbian character and her ordeal with coming into herself with </span>
  <span id="freeText6970554168934859704" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><br /><br /><b>I usually hate love triangles, I usually hate the romance. This book is different in that I actually enjoyed both.</b> I felt the love triangle was complex enough, the romance and relationships between the characters were beautifully, realistically portrayed. This book had a tremendous amount of humor. It had an amazing, strong main character. The side characters were compelling; funny, flawed, loveable. It portrayed a lesbian character and her ordeal with coming into herself with sensitivity, tact, and realism. The writing is awesome; I am going to have to restrain myself from using an abundance of quotes here.<br /><br />So why not a 4? Why not a 5? <b>Because as much as I loved the characters and the romance...both completely eclipsed the story. This is one of those rare instances where I loved the characters, but hated the slowness of the book.</b><br /><br />Because the angst was overwhelming. <br /><br />Because the plot was tedious, slow, and boring compared to brilliant portrayal of the characters.<br /><br />This book truly is good. It is so beautifully written. There was something on almost every page that made me smile, but the characters and the romance overshadowed the actual story. As much as I enjoyed the writing, as short as this book is, this book took me over an entire month to read because the actual plot line was not compelling at all. <b>This still remains a refreshing book, and I would still highly recommend it, because for me, excellent characterization wins out every time.</b><br /><br /><i>Untold</i> is the second book in the Lynburn Legacy. I don't recall much from the first book, but the beginning of this book summed up the events of the first book very well, however, it's probably best not to dive into this book without reading the first. Kami's link to Jared has been broken. Jared and Ash are both acting like children wrestling over a beloved toy. Most importantly; the sorcerer Rob Lynburn is back, and he plans to take over the town of Sorry-in-the-Vale.<br /><br />The plot is simple. The characters are not. The story drags on so much in the first half of the book; that's actually the part of the book that gave me so much pause in between my bouts of reading. <b>As funny the writing is, as compelling the characters, the plot moves at the pace of a spilled bottle of frozen molasses.</b><br /><br />The characters and the writing are without a doubt, the best thing about this book. <b>I could hardly turn a page without reading something that made me smile.</b> Kami is such an awesome character, as are the supporting casts. It still remains Kami's story, the narration is primarily from her point of view, and I absolutely adored her. She is suffering from the severance of her mental link to Jared, who now acts like he hates her.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Been chatting much with Jared?”<br />“We often have special moments where I come into a room and he immediately leaves,” Kami said. “I treasure those times.”</i>
</blockquote>It may feel silly, it may feel like an abundance of adolescent love, but for me, Kami and Jared's mental connection, and the anguish that results from the cutting of that connection felt so real; I understood Kami's pain. I also understood, to a lesser extent, why Jared acts out so much afterwards.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Every dark moment you ever had in your life,” Jared said. “Every time you were a kid hiding under the covers convinced that nobody in the world existed, that it was just you and the nightmares. Every time you felt alone in a crowd, alone by yourself, forever and essentially alone, and don’t pretend there weren’t moments like that. Every time you felt worthless, every time you thought there was no purpose to existing, no center to the world and no peace to be found. I never had a single moment like that, I was never lonely a day of my life, until now. Now I feel like the world is hell, and hell is a place where the souls of the damned can still see heaven. Because that’s the worst thing of all. And yet I can’t look away.”</i>
</blockquote>And rest assured, Jared DOES act out afterwards. There is a horrifying amount of angst throughout the book regarding Ash and Jared. They both have feelings of insecurity. They both have feelings of anger. They feel inadequate. They both like Kami. Jared reacts by running away. By pushing Kami away. By reacting in anger. By being barely civil.<br /><br />Ash reacts by crying.<blockquote>
  <i>Ash ran then, stumbling as if he was drunk or blind, through the home of his dreams and out into the night. He ran down the path into the dark woods, until he could no longer see the lit windows of the manor on the hill. Then he sat at the foot of a tree, head in his hands, and wept.</i>
</blockquote>They're both in a very confusing relationship with Kami, and there's an incident of mistaken-identity kissing in the dark that I found rather amusing. <blockquote>
  <i>“You thought?” Angela repeated. “Like, you had a kissing hallucination?”<br />“It was in the corridor,” Kami said. “It was dark. I thought it was Jared but it might—it might have been Ash.”<br />Angela blinked. “Excuse me? Might?”<br />“One of those mistaken-identity makeouts,” Kami said defensively. “They happen.”</i>
</blockquote>I really liked the love triangle here, and I usually cannot tolerate love triangles at all. <b>My problem is not the love triangle itself, but rather, how much precendence it took over the actual plot.</b><br /><br />The romance is sweet, steamy at times. <b>There is no sex, but there is plenty of heat, and I have to admit, I got quite hot under the collar at some of the barely repressed kissing scenes in this book.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Her fingers trailed light along the line of his collarbone, nails tracing the dip at the base of his throat, and she felt the shudder run through his body. She curled her fingers in under the collar of his shirt and used her hold to pull him in again.<br />They kissed and kissed, shivering and shaking apart, neither of them daring to touch each other anywhere risky, both scared and trying not to scare the other off.</i>
</blockquote>The other characters in the book are so, so well done. There are a lot of people involved, and they all have their distinct personality. I loved them all. Angela, Holly, Rusty. Instead of leaving them sidelined, they all have their roles to play in the book, and I grew to love them as much as I did Kami. They have such personality, they have such humor. None of the characters are perfect. They react foolishly sometimes, they run away and hurt others in stressful situations; but for me, that's what makes them so much more <b>real</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>She was desperate to be hurt or used or anything, as long as she wanted it, as long as she could prove it was only this she wanted.</i>
</blockquote>I loved the portrayal of Angela's sexuality in this book. Angela is a lesbian. She is in love with Holly, who does not exactly return her feelings. I felt that the portrayal of Angela's hurt, her confusion about her feelings were so well done. I loved the conversation she and Kami have about sexuality. It was never preachy. It is never out of place in the book. They're just two friends having a rather awkward conversation; they still love each other, they're still best friends. It's just something they need to discuss. The portrayal of Holly's feelings were so well done as well. Just because someone professes love to you doesn't mean the feeling is reciprocated, and I understand and sympathized with Holly's hurt, her confusion, her anger.<br /><br /><b>Bravo to Ms. Brennan for a compassionate, realistic portrayal of teenaged sexuality and coming out of the closet.</b><br /><br />Wonderfully written book, I just wished the plot was more compelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6970554168934859704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_458295116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458295116" />
    <a title="Danielle." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7005742-danielle"><img alt="Danielle." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506227599p2/7005742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458295116?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle." href="/user/show/7005742-danielle">Danielle.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458295116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8090806119904812610"><b>"[...] hell is a place where the souls of the damned can still see heaven."</b><br/> <br/>Once again, Sarah doesn't fail to impress and amaze me. <br/> <br/>Damn you for messing with my <b>feels</b> like this, Sarah. Damn you.<br/> <br/>In a small sleepy town called Sorry-in-the-Vale (with symbolic locations named Shadownchurch Lane, Pleasant Street, Sorrier River, Hope Field, Really Depressed Quarry, and more), things are not going as planned. After finding out that an evil sorcerer with a not-so-hidden-agenda named Rob was behind the</span>
  <span id="freeText8090806119904812610" style="display:none"><b>"[...] hell is a place where the souls of the damned can still see heaven."</b><br> <br>Once again, Sarah doesn't fail to impress and amaze me. <br> <br>Damn you for messing with my <b>feels</b> like this, Sarah. Damn you.<br> <br>In a small sleepy town called Sorry-in-the-Vale (with symbolic locations named Shadownchurch Lane, Pleasant Street, Sorrier River, Hope Field, Really Depressed Quarry, and more), things are not going as planned. After finding out that an evil sorcerer with a not-so-hidden-agenda named Rob was behind the death of Nicola Prendergast in <i>Unspoken</i>, it's Journalist Kami's duty to let the people of Sorry-in-the-Vale know that magic exist... with the help of a few Lynburns and some friends, of course.<br><br><b>"Let’s not front. We all know magic is real.<br><br>You know. Or it’s time you knew. It’s time someone told you.<br><br>I always said that every town has a story, that even our sleepy Sorry-in-the-Vale must have one. I was so sure that I could find a story hidden somewhere under the chocolate-box prettiness of our town. I thought finding a story would be like bird-watching in the Vale woods, waiting for bright eyes and a burst of wings. I thought it would be like finding gold.<br><br>It wasn’t like that at all.”</b><br><br>The task will not be easy. Quirky Kami will not only be encountering Scarecrows coming to life, betrayals, and the cold horrifying truth of Rob's plan, but she will experience love as well as the meaning of sacrifice.<br> <br>After reading reviews of disappointment, I can wipe my forehead of its perspiration from nervousness. I enjoyed Untold just as much as the first instalment; however, I can understand why readers were disappointed with this: the angst and misunderstandings. There was so much of it that even I was shaking the book and yelling aloud in annoyance! This may be the book’s greatest downfall. Nevertheless, I’m letting this slide due to the fact Unspoken left off with a jaw-dropping cliffhanger that had to continue its way in the second book of the Lynburn Legacy trilogy. Since this is the second book, everything (all the angst and anger and explanations) needs to be let out here; I feel that all of angst will not be present in the the third novel. <br><br>Untold goes into depth with the research, knowledge, and magic — readers will be reading stories of the Lynburn family and their past. <br><br>"It’s time to choose sides…"<br><br>Rob wants to return Sorry-in-the-Vale back to the way it used to be in the past: when sorcerer’s ruled and had the people in submission; occasionally drawing blood to enhance their power. But in order to do so he’ll need a blood sacrifice on the winter solstice… a human sacrifice. Kami, Ash*, Jared, Angela, Rusty, Holly, and Lillian does not want this to happen, so they’re making plans to fight back.<br><br>I enjoyed reading about this gothic town. The writing was so vivid and atmospheric. I also loved the small conversations here and there between Kami and Angela about Angela’s sexual orientation. Kami is there for her and never judgmental which I really liked; she didn’t see Angela differently. Though there’ll be problems with Holly and Angela that I found really frustrating. I’ll see how all of that turns out in the final book. There is some character development in here, but not much, which is fine. <br><br>Untold is an excellent Halloween read: outrageously funny and deliciously gothic.<br><br>I honestly have no idea what to do with life now that I’m finished with this book.<br><br>* I hated Ash so much in this one. What a little coward! I can’t go into details without spoiling, but you’ll find out soon enough once you’ve read this. I really hope he changes and develops in the next book. (Shakes my head)<br><br>*****************************************<br><br><b>PRE-REVIEW:</b><br><br><br>EDIT APRIL 23, 2013 <br><br>IT HAS A COVER OMMMMMMMGGGGGGG FREAKING OUT IN THE LIBRARY RIGHT NOW OK<br><br>-------<br><br><b>I just read the <a href="http://sarahtales.livejournal.com/204819.html" rel="nofollow noopener">snippet....</a></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298666ra/686643.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dearest Sarah:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378908ra/734891.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Jared looked down at her. “Want to go up to my room?”<br><br>Holly said, “Yes.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398002ra/768671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Kami...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371389ra/724432.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_400430986" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400430986" />
    <a title="Emily (Falling for YA)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya"><img alt="Emily (Falling for YA)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551209496p2/4788621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400430986?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily (Falling for YA)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily (Falling for YA)" href="/user/show/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya">Emily (Falling for YA)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375870422" href="/book/show/17061490-untold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya?shelf=waiting-on-wednesday">waiting-on-wednesday</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya?shelf=books-on-shelf-in-idaho">books-on-shelf-in-idaho</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400430986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13792896546630739874">Oh Sarah, I see what you're doing. Give us an amazing book, leave us on a terrible cliffhanger, make us wait until <s>June</s> September.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380389025ra/749963.gif' width='80%' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm on to you lady.<br/><br/><b>Official Review now that the above waiting madness is over:</b><br/>I loved Unspoken beyond all reason. My review is nothing but gushing sentences and stress. The cliffhanger at the end was a doozey and I don’t know how I managed to wait over a year to read Untold, but I did, and now I’m tasked with scooping up my feels and sorting them in to a coherent revi</span>
  <span id="freeText13792896546630739874" style="display:none">Oh Sarah, I see what you're doing. Give us an amazing book, leave us on a terrible cliffhanger, make us wait until <s>June</s> September.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380389025ra/749963.gif" width="80%" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm on to you lady.<br><br><b>Official Review now that the above waiting madness is over:</b><br>I loved Unspoken beyond all reason. My review is nothing but gushing sentences and stress. The cliffhanger at the end was a doozey and I don’t know how I managed to wait over a year to read Untold, but I did, and now I’m tasked with scooping up my feels and sorting them in to a coherent review. <br><br>Untold begins soon after Unspoken ended and Kami and Jared are not speaking, barely tolerating one another and both of them are absolutely miserable. They, along with the rest of the crew, must band together to stop Ash’s father from taking over Sorry-in-the-Vale and reinstituting blood sacrifices. The group spends a lot of time making plans, having planning meetings, training for said plan etc. and that is the reason I was unable to give this book 5 stars. The plot itself is not this books strong suit. There is so much waiting around for a final battle that when the battle does happen I felt rather unimpressed.<br><br>What this book does well, and what Sarah does well, is characters. I adore Kami who has taken her fledging journalism career in her own hands and is passing out a school paper that the entire town is reading. I love that she is strong, spunky, and despite not having any magical power she is the one actively trying to save the town, it is Kami that the others are following and looking to for direction. Even if Kami is a jumbled mess over Jared.<br><br>Jared disappointed me a little in this book. I won’t lie I’ve never been firmly in Jared’s corner. The brooding bad boy act is a little old, and while I do want him and Kami to be together his actions make it hard for me to like him. Jared and Kami kept having these ‘two ships passing in the night’ moments and after a while I wanted to shake them both. Say what you mean, and mean what you say!<br><br>Luckily, Rusty played a much bigger role in this novel and that almost entirely made up for my frustration with Kami and Jared. When I met Sarah at the RT Convention this year she asked me what team I was on and instantly and unabashedly I said “Team Rusty of course!” The guy is a total scene stealer and I liked that he is a little more serious (though still witty and awesome) in this novel. I hope to see even more of him in the next novel.<br><br>I almost forgot to mention Angela, Holly, and Ash so to quickly recap. Angela was great. I like her nearly as much as her brother. I’ve never really liked Holly so I didn’t like her in this book either. I could rant on about why I dislike her but honestly I don’t have a very good reason, she is just a character I don’t like. I found myself wondering why Kami is friends with her in the first place and I drew a blank. Then Ash, he reminds me of Amelia Pond in Doctor Who, he is the boy who waited; the one who’s done everything right and just wants to be noticed and loved. I feel so sorry for/sympathetic toward Ash I want him to have a happy ending because the guy is trying so damn hard and no one ever seems to notice or give him credit for that. <br><br>Overall, Untold was a novel I enjoyed. I didn’t like it as much as Unspoken. I felt the plot was a bit repetitive with all the planning and preparations but I was so happy to see the characters again that it was worth the wait. I am now going to suffer through another year of waiting just to read more about these characters and Sorry-in-the-Vale and Rusty, but mostly Rusty. <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13792896546630739874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The sorcerer concept is really cool along with the Gothicky vibe which is my favorite!<br /><br />Oh my, I wanted to shake Kami and Jared so many times! <div id="review_607276333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/607276333?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer607276333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16851456136654432210"><i>Hurls iPad across the room. Muffles a scream of frustration. Sighs and goes over to retrieve said iPad.</i><br/><br/>I absolutely hated this book (no, not really). It made me want to pull my hair out (seriously, I have bald spots). But for the "lovely, lovely readers who suffered over the ending of Unspoken," it's definitely a must-read. Yeah, I read your acknowledgement at the end of this book. I am on to you, lady!!! >:(<br/><br/>In Brennan's defense, my rating probably has to do a lot with my feelings toward Kami. T</span>
  <span id="freeText16851456136654432210" style="display:none"><i>Hurls iPad across the room. Muffles a scream of frustration. Sighs and goes over to retrieve said iPad.</i><br /><br />I absolutely hated this book (no, not really). It made me want to pull my hair out (seriously, I have bald spots). But for the "lovely, lovely readers who suffered over the ending of Unspoken," it's definitely a must-read. Yeah, I read your acknowledgement at the end of this book. I am on to you, lady!!! &gt;:(<br /><br />In Brennan's defense, my rating probably has to do a lot with my feelings toward Kami. Those who knew me when I read the ARC for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297412384" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken,</a> knows there I have NO lost love for her. Yep, she's still the sarcastic, nosy, self-righteous, "I'm going to find out the truth and write all about it" know-it-all that she has always been. And speaking of her "journalistic skills" - yes, it's in quotes - I'm NOT impressed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, she is NOT a journalist. Those stories are NOT how a real journalist would write. Maybe if you work for a tabloid. And you don't ever "coax" your sources into trusting you and spill all their secrets. And her "investigative" skills are mediocre at best. I still have a lot of questions about Matthew Cooper. And her taking-matters-into-her-own-hands usually end up creating a bigger mess. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just hate it when people like her give the stereotypically wrong impression of reporters. Sorry for the rant, but I just had to put that out there.<br /><br />Putting that part aside, Kami STILL annoyed me to no end. For someone who prided herself as a keen, observant journalist, she really was blind to everything that was going on and was really slow to catch up. I understand that she's lost a piece of herself, and she's unsure of what was real, but geez! Open your eyes! She has NO idea what she's talking bout, and she kept making assumptions instead of asking, leading to one stupid action after another.<br /><br />But, but, what happens between Kami and Jared? Do they get it together? I can't tell you. (Don't throw anything at me!) But I WILL tell you this - and you probably already guess it. Be prepared for those scenes where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they cross each other but on different sides of the streets or when one turns back to see the other walking away and finally turn back around only to find the other person turning back to see that person's retreating figure. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yep, leave your eReaders in their protective cases and style your hair in a ponytail or bun where it's hard to pull. But will it be all worth it in the end? You just have to read it and see.<br /><br />A few other issues before I get to the good stuff. The beginning of the book was so depressing to read. Jared was being a complete and utterly stoic jerk, and everyone was so mean. I really, really wanted to slap Holly. And Ash? What HAPPENED to him? I mean, I get that he was hiding his true nature in the first book, but seriously? To go from a pretty conniving villain to such a "bunny killer" in this book was so disappointing. It was pathetic really.<br /><br />Despite all of that, I still love Rusty, as I had claimed in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297412384" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken.</a> He's so goofy in a dorky kind of way that just makes me chuckle and shake my head. And he's pompous, but in a hilariously entertaining sort of way, not because he really thinks that much of himself. And it doesn't hurt that he's hot and very charming when it comes to the ladies. Swoon! It's just a shame that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he's not a love interest, although it would never work if he had been or ever will be. Although, I have a theory that Brennan did alluded to the fact that Kami does not know him quite as well as she thinks. I think Brennan is playing it safe because he's too brotherly, but she is trying to get a feel for what readers think of Rusty, which obviously, he does have some fans. I think I'm going to be upset if she does introduce him as an interest in the future. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, I still thought the story was pretty good, although it's nothing like the uniqueness of them being in each other's minds from book 1. There was a good mix of kick-butt action and learning about the magic, although I did have a pretty ridiculous image in my head <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[of them holding up bags while they're trying to fight each other. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The history of Matthew Cooper was really intriguing, and it makes you wonder if history had and possibly will repeat itself again. It was really interesting to see who was on which side, and it was gripping to see who was going to come out on top because you could never tell if Lillian or Rob had the upper hand.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, there were parts were I wanted to squee, and chapter 20 was an AWESOME chapter. But then, I had to suit up and go back onto the battlefield. And why did I throw my iPad? The end! OMG, the end! No, "lovely, lovely readers who suffered over the ending of Unspoken," there is not a cliffhanger. Ha suckers! Brennan is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["not that sorry… secretly a tiny bit glad…" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> :P But, but, still… Ah dangit, I can't spoil anything. Just read the book.<br /><br />I know this book had a lot of the usually drama that goes along with being the "middle book," which counts a lot to why my review seems so negative. But when I wasn't cursing at the story, I was flipping through the pages, really enjoying the book. I can tell that Brennan is just rounding everyone up for the next book, which is going to be explosive. Now, if only I can hang on long enough for this book to come out before the next one even has an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16851456136654432210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_715437786" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715437786" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715437786?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fucked-up-romance">fucked-up-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=hero-dick-to-heroine">hero-dick-to-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=cheating-hero">cheating-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=decent-secondary-characters">decent-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=douchery-afoot">douchery-afoot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=evul-people-are-evul">evul-people-are-evul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=teenagers-with-powers">teenagers-with-powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715437786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10810108102032001543"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>A somewhat entertaining read. There were a lot of parts that dragged but the main issue I had with <i>Untold</i> was that there was too much ridiculous teen drama, and not enough actual storyline. <br/><br/>-The characters were a bit of a mixed bag. I absolutely loathed Jared and Holly, they were fucking awful… Kami, Angela, and Rusty on the other hand were more or less decent enough. <br/><br/>-One thing that really irritated me was that most of the teen drama was down to a lack of communication. I hate when thin</span>
  <span id="freeText10810108102032001543" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />A somewhat entertaining read. There were a lot of parts that dragged but the main issue I had with <i>Untold</i> was that there was too much ridiculous teen drama, and not enough actual storyline. <br /><br />-The characters were a bit of a mixed bag. I absolutely loathed Jared and Holly, they were fucking awful… Kami, Angela, and Rusty on the other hand were more or less decent enough. <br /><br />-One thing that really irritated me was that most of the teen drama was down to a lack of communication. I hate when things are dragged out or angsty just because certain characters can't hold a simple fucking conversation — all it does is make everything come across as contrived and ridiculous.<br /><br />-Some of the writing and dialogue was awkward, and there were parts that didn't flow very well. <br /><br />-For most of <i>Untold</i> there wasn't much going on plot wise. Rob and his evul sorcerers threatened Kami and co at the beginning, and then Kami and the gang half heartedly tried to find ways to beat the bad guys whilst whining about their love lives, and the showdown at the end was utterly underwhelming. There was way too much misunderstandings, angst, and relationship nonsense… And not enough meaty plot.<br /><br />-Kami was a decent enough heroine (mostly). What did piss me off about her was like all other YA heroines she kept jumping to conclusions, and instead of talking to her friends (Jared mainly), she kept things to herself and created unnecessary drama.<br />I did like that Kami had a strong bond with her family and some of her friends — most heroines tend to be loners or misunderstood idiots, so it was nice having a heroine who didn't act all speshul and emo. <br />I did find it weird how Kami appointed herself the leader and took charge of trying to find ways to stop Rob and his evul sorcerers. She wasn't magical or knowledgeable, yet Jared/Ash and everyone else were cool about following her lead about things that she knew very little about. It wasn't like her investigative skills were all that great — it just made no sense whatsoever that her more powerful and more experienced friends were perfectly okay with letting Kami be in charge. <br />I was really disappointed by Kami's calm reaction when she stumbled upon Jared and Holly's hot and heavy make out session, it was weird how quickly she got over it. Not only that, it was super pathetic how she jumped into a relationship with Jared so soon after him hooking up with Holly - why would she want him a couple of days after he was all over one of her best friends? Where was her self respect?<br /><br />-Jared was such a whiny-self-pitying-selfish-bitchy-douche. He treated Kami like dirt and then whined when she didn't worship the ground he walked on. No matter how many times he claimed to have feelings for her it never rang true — not once did he actually act like he loved her. He didn't respect her, he ignored her, he told her he hated her, and he bitched at her. He showed more respect, passion and feeling towards Holly - he was all over her in the pub and it was obvious how desperate he was for some Holly action. His sudden 'I love Kami' mantra was ridiculous — he hadn't done anything that supported that statement. All he ever did around Kami was act like a bitch, and since when does that equal love?<br />Ugh, I HATED Jared. Kami deserved better than that fucking fucker.<br /><br />-Holly was a horrible friend. I felt sorry for her in regard to her family situation and the secrets she had to keep, but I hated how she was all over Ash and Jared when she knew that Kami once liked Ash, and that Kami was in love with Jared. There was no excuse for it, her being in a difficult situation didn't mean it was okay for her to stab Kami in the back just to make herself better. What kind of friend does that? Kami was nothing but supportive of her, and even Angela made it clear that she'd help Holly with anything. But because Holly was a selfish cow, she rejected them and chose to fuck over Kami because she was a vile cow.<br />I HATED how Holly treated Angela. She knew that Angela was having a difficult time with her sexuality and instead of being there for her… She acted disgusted. I hope Holly doesn't suddenly realise she wants Angela - I don't want Angela dating someone who treated her like rubbish and acted like she had a disease of some sort. Angela deserves better than a cow who's done nothing but hurt her. <br /><br />-Ash was meh. I didn't really see the point of him. Kami and co should have told him to fuck off after what he did in the first book, he didn't deserve to have any friends. Angela should have killed him or at the very least seriously hurt him - I don't know how she could be in the same room as him when he'd been planning to killing her.<br /><br />-I knew Ash and Jared would turn out to be half brothers.<br /><br />-I loved Rusty, he was really funny. He was definitely more suited to Kami than Jared. I really want a Rusty/Kami HEA. <br /><br />-Angela was as likeable as ever. Her friendship with Kami was really sweet. She definitely needs a new love interest, I don't want her settling for Holly after all the shit that happened between them. She needs someone that actually respects and appreciates her.<br /><br />-Kami and co were never in any lessons and they didn't seem to do any school work. They should have at least been a little bit busy with assignments and studying - instead all they did was sleuth, angst, whine, and fight evul.<br /><br />-That whole Matthew arc seemed pointless. I'm guessing there'll be some Matthew related discovery in the next book. I really don't know why there was so much time wasted on it in this book - the Matthew arc went nowhere.<br /><br />-Where did Kami's mum disappear to at the end?<br /><br />-Some parts seemed really preachy and heavy handed in regard to sexuality and whatnot.<br /><br />-I have no doubt that Rob will break Jared in the next book, and Jared will be all cold and evul for a while, he'll hurt Kami and co in some way, and then Kami will try to save him, and at the last minute he'll join the god guys, and all his douchey behaviour will be forgiven. Ugh, I hope he dies.<br /><br />All in all, it was a decent enough read, it just needed to be less teen-drama centric and more plot centric.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10810108102032001543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7461563790571950750" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/11/review-untold-by-sarah-rees-brennan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted at Writer of Wrongs</a><br><br><b>Untold by Sarah Rees Brennan, book two in the Lynburn Legacy: A Reading Experience</b><br><br><b>Me, upon beginning: </b>Oh, and everything's already gone to pot.<br><br><b>Me: </b>Best cameo made by a fleet of inanimate objects suddenly made animate.<br><br><b>Me: </b>KAMI YOU ARE SO SPECIAL DON'T YOU SEE HE'S LYING HE JUST CAN'T DEAL WITH HIS GOOEY MARSHMALLOW CENTER<br><br><b>Me:</b> *sob* I love a boy with layers. You, Jared Lynburn, are an onion. You're an onion parfait. Layered between many more onion parfaits.<br><br><b>Me:</b> I love the magic in this series. And the Britishness. And the boys. And the girls. And Kami. And the boys.<br><br><b>Me:</b> Can I grow up to be Lillian Lynburn<br><br><b>Me:</b> No, I want to be Jon Glass, I've changed by mind<br><br><b>Me:</b> Oh dear God that is the best and worst kiss scene in Creation<br><br><b>Me: </b>OMG PUNCHES ARE FLYING RUSTY OH MY GOD<br><br><b>Me:</b> Poor Holly. Mostly kiss, obviously!<br><br><b>Me:</b> SRB why do heap such pain on the sparkly little gem that is Kami she should know nothing but joy you monster<br><br><b>Me:</b> Jared, you colossal idiot.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381345527ra/4735585.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Me:</b> JARED AND KAMI YOU'RE PERFECT WHY CAN'T YOU SEEE IT, YOU HAVE SHARED A SOUUUUL, YOU ARE TANGLED UP TOGETHER! YOU BLEED WHEN HE BLEEDS! *sobs* It's so be-e-eautiful!<br><br><b>Me:</b> Oh, Ash. Thou hast made a valiant effort. *pats Ash's head*<br><br><b>Me: </b>AWKWARD.<br><br><b>Delivery man, at the door:</b> Delivery!<br><br><b>Me: </b>THERE'S NO ONE HERE BY THAT NAME GO AWAY WE'RE READING<br><br><b>Father: </b>That's the Chinese food. I ordered Chinese.<br><br><b>Me:</b> Kami is JAPANESE.<br><br><b>Father:</b> You've been reading that book too long.<br><br><img height="400" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384023980i/6749449._SY540_.jpg" width="298" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b> </b><br><br><b>Me:</b> Rusty, dearest, I have a lovely couch right here you could nap on if you like. Oh, hell, don't make me ship another ship, SRB, please. My armada is getting a bit unwieldy. Stop being so adorable, Rusty. If you can.<br><br><b>Me: </b>You can't.<br><br><b>Me: </b>Kami is an absolutely splendid, sparkly, magical girl made of unicorns and happiness and pluck and sass and sunshine and I adore her beyond all reason.<br><br><b>Me: </b>We've been planning for a big showdown for a while. There had better be a MASSIVE SHOWDOWN COMING UP. <br><br><b>Me: </b>*howls with laughter* *builds shrine to Jon Glass, best father in Sorry-in-the-Vale, the east competition ever, considering he doesn't drink or sacrifice his children to increase the potency of his dark magic in the goal of subjugating an entire village to his will*<br><br><b>Me: </b>I didn't know it was possible to love a group of characters so fiercely.<br><br><b>Me:</b> WHOAAAA, HOLLY. That's an excellent twist!<br><br><b>Me: </b>There is definitely something quippy in the water in Sorry-in-the-Vale. Everybody is so (unbelievably, to be honest) witty. I would move there in a heartbeat. I'd totally take a murderous, power-hungry horde of sorcerers in exchange for the guarantee of daily banter and repartee.<br><br><b>Me: </b>Sometimes I read the jokes in this book and I wonder if my brain secretly wrote it without telling me. This is a book.<br><br>*massive showdown*<br><br><b>Me:</b> NO.<br><br><b>Me: </b>NOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO!!!!!<br><br><img height="187" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384023980ra/6749451.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Me:</b> NNNNNNNNNGHHHHH!!!<br><br><b>Friend, unfortunately nearby: </b>That was not a sound as yet made by humans.<br><br><b>Me:</b> BUGUHHHHHHH.<br><br><b>Friend:</b> Wait, that's the series with the hot sorceror boys who make jokes, and where everybody wants to kiss everybody else all the time, and, like, they're all miserable? The one that made you scream that one time?<br><br><b>Me: </b>*says nothing, as is dead*<br><br><i>End scene.</i></span>

<div id="review_697956496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697956496" />
    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327078-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357523905p2/2327078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697956496?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/2327078-k">K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375870422" href="/book/show/17061490-untold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=hit-me-in-the-heart">hit-me-in-the-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=21st-cent">21st-cent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-dys">fantasy-sci-fi-dys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=identity-and-psychology">identity-and-psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-fine-its-ya">ok-fine-its-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=slippery-as-waterweed">slippery-as-waterweed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=this-shelf-is-divine">this-shelf-is-divine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=surprise-bitch-i-m-good">surprise-bitch-i-m-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697956496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7868918604424871897">Sit down. I have a lot to say...<br/><br/>There have been much debate over Sarah Rees Brennan's second installment in her <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> trilogy. It had been so hyped up it almost jinxed itself. <i>Untold</i> has received giddy praise and somber criticism. So, which is it? Well, it's kind of both.<br/><br/><i>Untold</i> tells the aftermath of Kami and Co. after having discovered that it was Rob Lynburn who had been doing the massacring around not-so-sleepy-town Sorry-in-the-Vale. Now, he's recruiting to build an army. As is with</span>
  <span id="freeText7868918604424871897" style="display:none">Sit down. I have a lot to say...<br /><br />There have been much debate over Sarah Rees Brennan's second installment in her <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> trilogy. It had been so hyped up it almost jinxed itself. <i>Untold</i> has received giddy praise and somber criticism. So, which is it? Well, it's kind of both.<br /><br /><i>Untold</i> tells the aftermath of Kami and Co. after having discovered that it was Rob Lynburn who had been doing the massacring around not-so-sleepy-town Sorry-in-the-Vale. Now, he's recruiting to build an army. As is with most middle books, the basic premise is preparation. Kami needs to spread the word out to the people, to educate them and arm them of and against these evil magic doers. <br /><br />Plot-wise, the book suffered faintly -- I say faintly because I am unyielding in my fan-love and will be satisfied with whatever Brennan gives me. The book is slow and in the end, progress is short. We learn a little more about how magic works between the Lynburns, a few more spells, a bit more history. But somehow Kami spends more time learning karate moves, doing historical research and playing undercover agents -- all important but not quite the action readers were hoping for. Something I really liked, however, is the time spent with Kami's parents. It's a sweet relationship with genuine affection, so the downward spiral it descends into is heartbreaking. There is also more mystery with Kami's mom. The trouble is, we are given almost no answers.<br /><br />As for the paranormal factor in this novel, it <i>is</i> hard to believe that as a town that is in the midst of war between centuries-old sorcery and good old human mortality, there is still such a thing as school, or trick-or-treating, or going to the post office. This is one heck of a diplomatic and considerate war -- but I understand, that's the way of the game. With that said, it does make up for lost bloodshed. There is gore and appropriate repercussions are dispensed.<br /><br />Surprisingly, something many found exasperating was one of the highlights and strengths in the first book -- the quirky, eccentric yet lovable smart-alec attitude of the characters. I agree begrudgingly. Yes, they did occasionally meander into Annoying Ville. There were a little too many clever quips, too many droll retorts.<br /><br />Kami, in particular. Sometimes I just wanted her to speak normal, which is almost sacrilegious as she is one of the most colourful and effervescent protagonists I've ever met. More than that, she stands for self-respect and self-confidence. Her psychology, understandably, needs healing. She is still struggling from detaching herself as an individual from her link to Jared. Did all her guts and spirit come solely from him or did she possess them on her own? Essentially, is she herself without him? Jared, too, is beginning to open up. And near the end, we hear him; we are allowed access to a character who has so far been unreadable. It was such conflicting pleasure. (Only Jared can do that.)<br /><br />Having said that, they still frustrated me. Good god, the delusions! The angst! The misinterpretations! You see, the romantic core in the book, to me, is clear. It is just the journey there that is pissing me off. When it comes to love, these two are clueless. (But so meant to be.) The book is heavily focused on mending the cruel cracks left on them after the cut. And the scars go deep. And, as in <i>Unspoken</i>, it is painful yet so rewarding.<br /><br />This book doesn't quite reach the height of expectations -- and that's okay as they were Everest. But it is <i>still</i> spectacular. What I truly appreciate is the spectrum of topics Brennan covers in her paranormal romance thriller: homosexuality, family dysfunctions, the plight of low income families, marriage problems, superficial beauty, self-acceptance. It is all done subtly, softly; without ever becoming cumbersome.<br /><br />Brennan tells an absurd, fun, heartfelt story of a girl who speaks to a voice in her head. This voice turns out to be a real live boy. And while they wander into magical adventures, it is ultimately about so much more.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears on <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/10/untold-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7868918604424871897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_688406388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/688406388" />
    <a title="Isa Lavinia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1016831-isa-lavinia"><img alt="Isa Lavinia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518528816p2/1016831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/688406388?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isa Lavinia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isa Lavinia" href="/user/show/1016831-isa-lavinia">Isa Lavinia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=otp">otp</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer688406388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer937673343166126115"><br/><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/> <br/>First of all I should say the author was incredibly kind to send me this book - more accurately, my cat won this book for me, but that's a long story involving scratches, and forcing pets to wear little wire-framed spectacles.<br/> <br/>The fact I was sent this book by the author does not affect, in any way, my review.What does affect it, is that I've been following Sarah Rees Brennan's writing since way back when, and she has never, ever, disappointed me. So now here we are, the ~dreaded~ 2nd book </span>
  <span id="freeText937673343166126115" style="display:none"><br><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br> <br>First of all I should say the author was incredibly kind to send me this book - more accurately, my cat won this book for me, but that's a long story involving scratches, and forcing pets to wear little wire-framed spectacles.<br> <br>The fact I was sent this book by the author does not affect, in any way, my review.What does affect it, is that I've been following Sarah Rees Brennan's writing since way back when, and she has never, ever, disappointed me. So now here we are, the ~dreaded~ 2nd book of a trilogy. In my possession (I may have called it "my precious once or twice...") before it's even out.<br>Obviously I freaked out. Not in a "This is so great, I am so lucky! Yay!", but in a "Omg, what if I don't like it?!"<br> <br>It's terrible when you love an author's work and then they write something and you hate it! What now?! What if I hate it?!<br> <br>This brought me back to when my bff had a baby girl. I know you're supposed to say nice things the first time you see someone's baby, but the more I put it off, the more I stressed out over it: what if the baby was HIDEOUS? What if, when in the presence of that abomination unto the Lord all I could come up with would be something like, "Oh, she has... she has very hirsute whiskers!"<br>So I put it off and I kept training saying nice things in front of a mirror for a week straight. But finally I could put it off no longer and I had to go see the baby. And the baby was SO FREAKING CUTE!!! So cute I actually turned to the parents and expressed my relief on not having had to lie about her looks. Never do this, by the way - I’ve since learned it’s a social faux pas.<br> <br>Much the same situation happened with Untold. I was freaking out! I was composing polite ways to critique a disappointing book, because I love the author, and I love everything she writes, but maybe she would read my dreadful review and go, "This is it, the last drop! I shall never put pen to paper again, not even to sign my own name!"<br> <br>But joy of joys, Untold was much more amazing that my bff's baby. Don't tell her I said that! I mean the kid is really cute, but it just stayed in her crib, sleeping, which I admit, she did rather well... but...<br> <br>Untold, however, starts kind of like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432145i/867841.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Murderous scarecrows! Girl Power! Hot boys! Hot girls! And chocolate pasta: which I did not even know was a thing, if anyone can get me some I'll be yours forever.<br> <br>Seriously, this is Sarah Rees Brennan at her best!<br> <br>I read some reviews expressing displeasure at her use of humour, particularly during dramatic moments. That's what makes it work for me! You know how when you're with someone who'd been so important to you but now is not, and for a fleeting moment there's that spark where the old friendship is there and alive, and everything is well and we're all so happy- BUT IT'S NOT, because it was just a moment, and now it's back to bleak reality. Tell me that doesn't make the situation that more poignant: the juxtaposition of sadness and humour, it makes one so much sadder, the other so much more precious... It's genius writing, that's what it is!<br> <br>And major props for girl friendship! Passing the Bechdel test left, right, and centre!Plus intrigue, and girl sleuths, creepy magic, and awesome portrayals of family interactions.<br> <br>What more could I ask for?!<br>Make-out scenes, of course - but those are in there as well!!<br> <br>So, I know I talk (well, write) too much, and I usually don't make much sense, but if you take anything from this review it should be: GO READ UNTOLD AS SOON AS YOU CAN GET IT!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="937673343166126115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436275897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6853812531296116750"><b> Actual Rating 3.5</b><br/><br/>I have to say, I wasn't nearly as disappointed by this follow-up as I thought I would be but at the same time, it wasn't as awesome as Unspoken. For starters, Kami makes me feel a little iffy to be honest. I like her but at the same time, I really want to shake her.<br/><br/>Also the romance. Seriously? WHAT IS UP with Kami constantly thinking she isn't nearly as attractive as any of her friends and then you see that three guys are vying for her attention! WHAT THE WHAT? <br/><br/>Jared has to be </span>
  <span id="freeText6853812531296116750" style="display:none"><b> Actual Rating 3.5</b><br /><br />I have to say, I wasn't nearly as disappointed by this follow-up as I thought I would be but at the same time, it wasn't as awesome as Unspoken. For starters, Kami makes me feel a little iffy to be honest. I like her but at the same time, I really want to shake her.<br /><br />Also the romance. Seriously? WHAT IS UP with Kami constantly thinking she isn't nearly as attractive as any of her friends and then you see that three guys are vying for her attention! WHAT THE WHAT? <br /><br />Jared has to be one of the most frustrating love interests ever but at the same time, I absolutely love him. I love how complicated he is character is and I loved getting to know him better in this one. There is something to be said about a character who you could practically write an essay on as you peel back the layers.<br /><br />Anyway, I am looking forward to reading Unmade but I reallly hope the romantic drama won't get worse.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1184140906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184140906" />
    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35007929-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415626292p2/35007929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184140906?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/35007929-cody">Cody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184140906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12458177082246357805"><b>A Fabulous Follow Up</b><br/><br/>After the devastating cliffhanger of Unspoken I just HAD to start Untold straight away. <b>WARNING:</b> The cliffhanger to Untold is just as bad; seriously recommend having all 3 books before you start this series!<br/><br/>The evil sorcerer Rob Lynburn is back and eager to take over Sorry-in-the-Vale and bring back the old ways of sacrificing people to aid magic. Rob is now recruiting an army of sorcerer’s to overthrow his wife Lilian Lynburn and rule Aurimere Manor. The character’s are the </span>
  <span id="freeText12458177082246357805" style="display:none"><b>A Fabulous Follow Up</b><br /><br />After the devastating cliffhanger of Unspoken I just HAD to start Untold straight away. <b>WARNING:</b> The cliffhanger to Untold is just as bad; seriously recommend having all 3 books before you start this series!<br /><br />The evil sorcerer Rob Lynburn is back and eager to take over Sorry-in-the-Vale and bring back the old ways of sacrificing people to aid magic. Rob is now recruiting an army of sorcerer’s to overthrow his wife Lilian Lynburn and rule Aurimere Manor. The character’s are the biggest selling point of this series: Kami is as hilarious as ever, Jared as broody, Ash being insecure and Angela coming to terms with being a lesbian. Brennan managed to create a realistic view of being a teenager with different feelings and relationships.<br /><br />Kami is still her humorous self and had me laughing with some of her best quotes..<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Been chatting much with Jared?"<br />"We often have special moments where I come into a room and he immediately leaves," Kami said. "I treasure those times.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The love triangle takes on a whole new level now that Kami and Jared are no longer connected mentally and after the way he was at the end of Unspoken I needed to know how he really felt. The romance is filled with so much angst it’s frustrating but I secretly loved it especially when Jared &amp; Holly do something ridiculously stupid, I was fuming! Annnnd after that silly lapse in judgment I now have to deal with Kami linked to Ash? What is happening!<br />Brennan’s writing has significantly improved since Unspoken, I was able to follow and enjoy the story. It was slow and a little predictable but still executed wonderfully, I just hoped for a more exciting plot. With that said after that cliffhanger I cannot wait to read Unmade.<br /><br /><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12458177082246357805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
